والأنواع متنازلة إلى السافل ويسمّى نوع الأنواع، وما بينهما متوسطاتٍ مراتب الأنواع وذلك لأن جنس الجنس يكون أعم من الجنس، وهكذا إلى جنس لا جنس له فوقه وهو العالي وجنس الأجناس كالجوهر قوله :متنازلة بأن يكون التنزل من العام إلى الخاص؛ وذلك لأن نوع النوع يكون أخص من النوع وهكذا إلى أن ينتهي إلى نوع لا نوع له تحته له تحته وهو السافل ونوع الأنواع كالإنسان قوله وما بينهما متوسطات أي ما بين العالي والسافل في سلسلتي الأنواع والأجناس تسمى متوسطات، فما بين الجنس العالي والجنس السافل أجناس متوسطة، أعم: فالحيوان جنس وليس تحته جنس آخر؛ لأن تحته أنواعا حقيقية يمتنع كونها أجناسا والجسم النامي جنس وأعم له له منه فهو جنس الجنس وفوقه الجسم المطلق وهو جنس له وأعم منه وفوقه الجوهر الذي هو جنس ويسمي جنس الأجناس؛ فإن الجنسية تعرض للشيء باعتبار العموم، فما يكون أعم من الكل يسمى جنس الأجناس، لوجود كمال صفة الجنسية وليس هو إلا الجنس العالي، فيسمى به بخلاف نوع الأنواع؛ فإن النوعية باعتبار الخصوص، فما يكون الخصوصية فيه أكثر يوجد فيه صفة النوعية على الكمال، فهو اللائق لأن يسمى بنوع الأنواع، وهو النوع السافل؛ لأنه أخص من الكل. إسماعيل) وهكذا إلى جنس يعني لا بد من الانتهاء إليه، وإلا لزم تركب الماهية من مقولات لا تتناهى، فيتوقف تصورها على الإحضار كلها وهو محال؛ لأن إحاطة الذهن بأمور غير متناهية محال بالضرورة فيلزم أن لا يكون حقيقة من الحقائق معلومة وبطلانه أظهر من أن يخفى. (عبد) هكذا إلى أن ينتهي لأن الترتيب في الأنواع الإضافية لا يجري إلا باعتبار الخصوص، وأخص الكل يكون نوعا للكل ونوع الأنواع. (عبد) أجناس متوسطة إلخ واعلم أنه لما جرى عادة المنطقيين بتمثيل الجنس العالي بالجوهر والنوع السافل بالإنسان، وكان تحت الجوهر ثلاثة أجناس الجسم والجسم النامي والحيوان، وفوق الإنسان ثلاثة أنواع: الحيوان والجسم النامي والجسم، سموا الجنس العالي جنس الأجناس؛ لأنه فوق ثلاثة أجناس والنوع السافل نوع الأنواع؛ لأنه تحت ثلاثة أنواع، ولما كان المتوسط بين العالي والسافل من الأجناس والأنواع زائدة على واحد ويصح عندهم إطلاق لفظ الجمع على ما فوق الواحد قال المصنف: وبينهما متوسطات فلا يرد أنه لا يشرط التعدد فيما تحت الجنس العالي ولا فيما فوق النوع السافل ولا فيما بينهما، ولهذا إذا كان للماهية جنسان: قريب وبعيد فالبعيد جنس عال ويقال له أيضًا : جنس الأجناس اصطلاحا ولتلك الماهية نوع الأنواع وإن لم يكن فوقها إلا نوع واحد وهو الجنس القريب. (عبد) وما بين النوع العالي والنوع السافل أنواع متوسطة، هذا إن رجع الضمير إلى مجرد العالي والسافل، وإن عاد إلى الجنس العالي والنوع السافل المذكورين صريحا كان المعنى أن ما بين الجنس العالي والنوع السافل متوسطات، إما جنس متوسط فقط كالنوع العالي، أو نوع متوسط فقط كالجنس السافل، أو جنس متوسط ونوع متوسط معا كالجسم النامي. ثم اعلم أن المصنف لم يتعرض للجنس المفرد والنوع المفرد إما لأن الكلام فيما يترتب والمفرد ليس داخلا في سلسلة الترتيب وإما لعدم تيقن وجودهما كالنوع العالي كالجسم؛ لأنه جنس متوسط؛ لأن فوقه جنسا، وهو الجوهر وتحته جنسا وهو الجسم النامي وليس بنوع متوسط؛ إذ ليس فوقه نوع بل فوقه جنس عال عبد كالجنس السافل: كالحيوان؛ فإنه نوع متوسط؛ لأن فوقه نوعا وهو الجسم النامي وتحته نوعا وهو الإنسان وليس بجنس متوسط؛ لأنه وإن كان فوقه جنس لكن ليس تحته جنس بل تحته نوع سافل. (عبد) ثم اعلم جواب عما يقال: إن مولانا الكابتي صاحب الشمسية وغيره جعلوا مراتب الأجناس والأنواع أربعا : يجعل الجنس المفرد والنوع المفرد قسما رابعا و لم يتعرض المصنف محله للجنس المفرد والنوع المفرد.(عبد) والمفرد فإن الجنس الداخل في سلسلة الترتيب إما أن يكون عاليا فيكون تحته ،جنس، وإما أن يكون سافلا فيكون فوقه جنس، وإما أن يكون متوسطا فيكون فوقه وتحته جنس وكذا حال النوع، فيمتنع أن يدخل النوع المفرد والجنس المفرد في سلسلة الترتيب. (إسماعيل) وجودهما: اعلم أنهم لما نظروا إلى مفهوم الجنس المفرد والنوع المفرد وجدوها صالحا لأن يقع في نفس الأمر لكنهم لما تفصحوا للمثال لم يتهيأ لهم مثال في الواقع، ففرضوه؛ ليسهل به التفهيم والتفهم، فمثال الجنس المفرد: العقل إذا فرض أن الجوهر ليس جنسا له بل هو عرض عام، والعقول العشرة الداخلة تحته مختلفة الحقائق أنواع لكن كلا منها منحصر في فرد واحد كالشمس، ومثال النوع المفرد: العقل أيضًا إذا فرض أن الجوهر جنس للعقل وليس للجوهر جنس والعقول العشرة أشخاص له متفقة الحقيقة فوجودهما ليس بمتيقن؛ فإن هذين الفرضين يمتنع اجتماعهما في الواقع، وإلا لزم اجتماع المتنافيين. إسماعيل)
And the species descend to the lowest, and it is called the species of species, and what is between them are intermediates in the ranks of species. That is because the genus of a genus is more general than the genus, and so on until [one reaches] a genus that has no genus above it, which is the highest, and the genus of genera like 'substance'. He said: 'descending' meaning the descent from the general to the particular; that is because the species of a species is more specific than the species, and so on until it ends at a species that has no species below it, which is the lowest, and the species of species like 'human'. He said: 'and what is between them are intermediates' meaning what is between the highest and the lowest in the two series of species and genera are called intermediates. So between the highest genus and the lowest genus are intermediate genera. More general: animal is a genus and no other genus is below it because below it are real species which cannot be genera; and the growing body is a genus, and more general than it is absolute body which is a genus for it and more general than it, and above it is substance which is a genus and is called the genus of genera. For genus-ness occurs to a thing by virtue of generality, so what is most general of all is called genus of genera, due to the perfection of the attribute of genus-ness, and it is nothing but the highest genus, so it is called by that. Contrary to species of species, for species-ness is by virtue of particularity, so what has more particularity has the attribute of species-ness perfectly, so it is fitting to be called species of species, and it is the lowest species because it is most particular of all. (Isma'il) 'And so on to a genus' means it must end at it, otherwise the quiddity would be composed of infinite categories, and its conception would depend on bringing them all to mind, which is impossible because the mind's encompassing of infinite things is impossible necessarily, so it would follow that no reality is known, and its falsity is more obvious than to be hidden. ('Abd) 'Thus until it ends' because the order in relative species only proceeds by virtue of particularity, and the most particular of all is a species for all and species of species. ('Abd) 'Intermediate genera etc.' And know that since the custom of logicians is to represent the highest genus by 'substance' and the lowest species by 'human', and under substance are three genera: body, growing body, and animal, and above human are three species: animal, growing body, and body, they named the highest genus 'genus of genera' because it is above three genera, and the lowest species 'species of species' because it is below three species. And since the intermediate between the highest and the lowest, from the genera and species, exceeds one, and according to them it is valid to apply the plural form to what exceeds one, the author said: 'and between them are intermediates'. So it is not objected that multiplicity is not a condition for what is under the highest genus nor for what is above the lowest species nor for what is between them. For this reason, if a quiddity has two genera, proximate and remote, the remote is a high genus and is also called 'genus of genera' terminologically, and that quiddity has a species of species even if above it there is only one species, which is the proximate genus. ('Abd) And between the high species and the low species are intermediate species. This is if the pronoun refers to just the high and the low. But if it refers explicitly to the high genus and the low species mentioned, the meaning would be that what is between the high genus and the low species are intermediates: either only an intermediate genus like the high species, or only an intermediate species like the low genus, or both an intermediate genus and an intermediate species together like the growing body. Then know that the author did not address the singular genus and the singular species, either because the discussion is about what is ordered and the singular is not included in the series of order, or because their existence is not certain. Like the high species like body; for it is an intermediate genus because above it is a genus, substance, and below it is a genus, growing body, and it is not an intermediate species since there is no species above it, rather above it is a high genus. ('Abd) Like the low genus like animal; for it is an intermediate species because above it is a species, growing body, and below it is a species, human, and it is not an intermediate genus because although there is a genus above it, there is no genus below it, rather below it is a low species. ('Abd) Then know, in response to what is said: That our master al-Kabati, author of al-Shamsiyya, and others made the ranks of genera and species four: they consider the singular genus and the singular species as a fourth division, and the author in his place did not address the singular genus and the singular species. ('Abd) And the singular: the genus that enters the series of order is either high, so there is a genus below it; or low, so there is a genus above it; or intermediate, so there is a genus above and below it. Similarly for the species. So it is impossible for the singular species and the singular genus to enter the series of order. (Isma'il) Their existence: Know that when they looked at the concept of singular genus and singular species, they found them valid to occur in actual reality, but when they researched for an example, they did not find a real example, so they hypothesized one to facilitate teaching and understanding. An example of singular genus: intellect, if we suppose that substance is not a genus for it but rather a common accident, and the ten intellects under it are of different realities as species, but each is restricted to one individual like the sun. An example of singular species: intellect also, if we suppose that substance is a genus for intellect and substance has no genus, and the ten intellects are individuals for it of the same essence. So their existence is not certain, for these two suppositions cannot coexist in reality, otherwise two contradictories would coexist. (Isma'il)
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of genera (ajnas) and species (anwa') within the framework of the five universals. The author explains that genera and species form hierarchical chains: genera descend from the most general (jins al-ajnas, e.g. substance) to the most specific (al-jins al-safil), and species ascend from the most specific (naw' al-anwa', e.g. human) to the most general (al-naw' al-'ali). Between the extremes lie intermediate genera and species. The commentator emphasizes the necessity of a highest genus to avoid infinite regress: if there were no ultimate genus, the quiddity (mahiyya) would be composed of an infinite series of categories, making conception impossible. The typical example from logicians is used: substance as highest genus, with body, growing body, animal as intermediate genera, and human as lowest species. The discussion then addresses the singular genus and singular species (al-jins al-mufrad, al-naw' al-mufrad), which are not part of the ordering series because they lack the required relative relations; they are only hypothetical.

الجنس المفرد
النوع المفرد
سلسلة الترتيب

Defining Differentia and the Role of 'Ayyu Shay'in'
Author defines differentia and explains the function of 'ayyu shay'in'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define differentia as the universal that answers 'what thing is it in its essence?' and distinguish its interrogative function from that of genus.

Core Idea
Differentia tells you what kind of thing something is within its genus.

In this lesson, we explore the third of the five universals: the differentia (fasl). The passage defines differentia and explains how the interrogative phrase 'ayyu shay'in' is used to request it. Understanding this distinction is essential for constructing precise definitions in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate 'الفصل' in the Arabic. The author states it is 'what is predicated of a thing in answer to "what thing is it in its essence?"'. This is the core definition.
2
Understand the interrogative role
The word 'أي' is used to request what distinguishes a thing from others that share its genus. In the example, seeing an animal from afar prompts the question 'أي شيء هو?' to learn its differentia.
Contrast with 'ما هو' which asks for the genus.
3
Extract the genus and differentia of differentia itself
The differentia's genus is 'المقول على الشيء' (what is predicated of a thing). Its differentia is being 'في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته' (in answer to 'what thing is it in its essence?'). This distinguishes it from other universals.
4
Apply the concept to an Islamic example
Consider the definition of 'human' (insan). Its genus is 'animal' (hayawan) and its differentia is 'rational' (natiq). The question 'ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatih?' would be answered by 'rational'.
This shows how differentia completes a definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of the third universal, the differentia (fasl). Differentia is what is said in response to the question 'ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatih?' (what thing is it in its essence?), and it serves to distinguish the thing from others that share its genus. The commentator explains the function of the interrogative word 'ayyu': it is used to request the property that differentiates the thing from its co-sharing species. An example is given: if you see something from a distance and know it is an animal, you then ask 'ayyu shay'in huwa?' to know whether it is a horse, a man, etc., and the differentia (like rational) distinguishes it. The passage is a concise introduction to the role of differentia in definition.

The Differentia: Definition and Resolution of al-Razi's Objection
Author defines fasl and resolves its confusion with hadd and jins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the differentia from the genus and complete definition in any Islamic logical definition, and explain why only the simple essential differentia answers 'what thing is it in its essence'.

Core Idea
The differentia alone directly distinguishes the essence; the genus and definition need it.

The differentia (fasl) is one of the five universals, and its precise definition is crucial for constructing correct definitions in Islamic sciences. The passage gives the definition and then faces a problem: if we ask 'what thing is man in his essence?' both 'rational animal' (the complete definition) and 'rational' (the differentia) seem to fit. Imam al-Razi raised this objection, and the passage resolves it by clarifying that the question seeks a simple essential distinguisher, which only the differentia provides. Understanding this resolution sharpens your ability to evaluate definitions in fiqh, usul, and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of differentia
The passage states: 'the differentia is what is said of a thing in answer to "what thing is it in its essence" if it distinguishes it.' Write down this definition and underline key terms: 'said of a thing', 'answer to what thing is it in its essence', 'distinguishes'.
2
Identify the problem: the definition seems to apply to hadd and jins
When we ask 'what thing is man in his essence?' we could answer 'rational animal' (the complete definition) or 'animal' (the genus). This means the definition of differentia would also be true of the complete definition and genus, which contradicts the fact that differentia is one of the five simple universals.
Imam al-Razi is cited as the source of this objection.
3
Analyze the resolution: what does 'what thing' truly seek?
The passage explains that the question seeks a simple essential distinguisher – something that distinguishes the essence directly without any intermediary. The genus (e.g., 'animal') distinguishes only through its differentia (e.g., 'sentient', 'growing'), and the complete definition distinguishes through its parts. Only the differentia itself meets the condition of being a simple essential distinguisher.
So the definition stands: only the differentia is the proper answer to 'what thing is it in its essence' when asked about the essence directly.
4
Apply the distinction to an Islamic example
Consider the definition of 'wudu' (ablution) in fiqh. A jurist might define it as 'an act of purification using water on specific body parts with intention'. Here the genus is 'act of purification', and the differentia is 'using water on specific body parts with intention'. When asked 'what thing is wudu in its essence?' the simple differentia that distinguishes it from other purifications (like ghusl or tayammum) is 'using water on specific body parts with intention'. The complete definition 'act of purification using water...' is not the differentia because it is composite.

(إسماعيل) وجودهما: اعلم أنهم لما نظروا إلى مفهوم الجنس المفرد والنوع المفرد وجدوها صالحا لأن يقع في نفس الأمر لكنهم لما تفصحوا للمثال لم يتهيأ لهم مثال في الواقع، ففرضوه؛ ليسهل به التفهيم والتفهم، فمثال الجنس المفرد: العقل إذا فرض أن الجوهر ليس جنسا له بل هو عرض عام، والعقول العشرة الداخلة تحته مختلفة الحقائق أنواع لكن كلا منها منحصر في فرد واحد كالشمس، ومثال النوع المفرد: العقل أيضًا إذا فرض أن الجوهر جنس للعقل وليس للجوهر جنس والعقول العشرة أشخاص له متفقة الحقيقة فوجودهما ليس بمتيقن؛ فإن هذين الفرضين يمتنع اجتماعهما في الواقع، وإلا لزم اجتماع المتنافيين. (إسماعيل) ثم قال: تعريف الفصل عن المشاركات في الجنس لكن ترددت في أنه هل هو إنسان أو فرس أو غيرهما، تقول: أي حيوان هذا؟ فيجاب بما يخصصه ويميزه عن مشاركاته في الحيوانية. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: إذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في ذاته" كان المطلوب ذاتيا من ذاتيات الإنسان يميزه عما يشاركه في الشيئية، فيصح أن يجاب بأنه حيوان ناطق، كما يصح أن يجاب بأنه ناطق، فيلزم صحة وقوع الحد في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، وأيضا يلزم أن لا يكون تعريف الفصل مانعا لصدقه على الحد، وهذا مما استشكله الإمام الرازي هو، كما مر. الإنسان: "الإنسان" مبتدأ أول وأي شيء" مبتدأ ثان "و "هو" خبره والجملة خبر المبتدأ الأول وقوله: "في ذاته"، ظرف مستقر في موضع الحال عن "هو" بتأويل أي شيء يميز معتبرا وملحوظا في ذاته مع قطع النظر عن عوارضه على مذهب من لا يجوز وقوعها عن المبتدأ وأما عند من جوزه فلا حاجة إلى التأويل. (عبد و إسماعيل) فيلزم ولم يقل به أحد بل إنما يجاب بالحد إذا سئل عن النوع بما هو . (إسماعيل) وأيضًا كما يلزم وقوع الحد التام في جواب أي شيء صح أنه لا يقع في جواب أي شيء بل يقع في جواب ما الحد فإن مجموع الحيوان الناطق حد يصدق حينئذ عليه أنه المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته مع أن الحد ليس بفصل؛ لأنه مركب من الفصل والجنس والمركب من الشيء وغيره مغاير لذلك الشيء، وأيضا الكليات الخمسة قسم للكلي المفرد لا المركب والحد مركب خارج عن الخمسة، فههنا إشكالان: الخلط وعدم مانعة تعريف الفصل بالحد (عبد) استشكله وينبغي تقرير الإشكال بأن المطلوب من أي شيء هو في ذاته إن كان ما يميز تميزا تاما يخرج الفصل البعيد عن تعريف الفصل، وإن كان ما يميز تميزا في الجملة فيصدق التعريف على الجنس والحد التام. وإلى هذا يشير قوله وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس والجواب على هذا التقرير عن هذا الإشكال أن المراد من الامتياز الامتياز بالذات في الجملة، فالمراد أن أي شيء يطلب المفرد المميز بالذات في الجملة وعلى هذا التقدير تعين الفصل في جواب أي شيء هو لا غير؛ فإن المفرد المميز بالذات ليس إلا الفصل، وأما الجنس فليس مميزا للماهية إلا بواسطة الفصل القريب، وفصله القريب فصل بعيد، فالمميز في الحقيقة فصل الماهية فإذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في جوهره ؟ فلا يقع في الجواب إلا الناطق؛ فإنه مميز بالذات لا بواسطة شيء آخر بخلاف الحيوان؛ فإنه وإن كان مميزا عن الجمادات والنباتات لكنه لا بالذات بل بواسطة فصل الإنسان وإن كان بعيدا هو النامي والحساس والحد مع أنه ليس بمفرد. يميز بواسطة الفصل أيضًا. (إسماعيل)
Definition of the third differentia: The differentia is what is said of a thing in answer to 'what thing is it in its essence?' if it distinguishes it... And between the high species and the low species are intermediate species, this if the pronoun refers to mere high and low, and if it refers to the high genus and low species explicitly mentioned, the meaning would be that between the high genus and low species are intermediates, either only intermediate genus like the high species, or only intermediate species like the low genus, or both intermediate genus and intermediate species like the growing body. Then know that the author did not address the single genus and single species either because the discussion is about what is ordered and the single is not included in the chain of order, or because their existence is not certain. His statement: 'any thing': Know that the word 'any' is used to ask for what distinguishes a thing from what shares with it in what this word is added to. For example: If you see something from afar and you are certain it is an animal... like the high species like body; because it is an intermediate genus; because above it is a genus, namely substance, and below it is a genus, namely growing body, and it is not an intermediate species; since there is no species above it but rather above it is a high genus. (Abd) And like the low genus: like animal; for it is an intermediate species; because above it is a species, namely growing body, and below it is a species, namely man, and it is not an intermediate genus; because although there is a genus above it, there is no genus below it but rather a low species. (Abd) Then know in answer to what is said: That our master al-Kabti, author of al-Shamsiyya, and others made the ranks of genera and species four: they make the single genus and single species a fourth division, and the author did not address in his place the single genus and single species. (Abd) And the single: for the genus included in the chain of order is either high, then below it is a genus, or low, then above it is a genus, or intermediate, then above and below it are genera, and similarly for species. So it is impossible for the single species and single genus to enter the chain of order. (Ismail) Their existence: Know that when they looked at the concept of single genus and single species, they found them valid to occur in reality, but when they searched for an example they could not find a real example, so they assumed it to facilitate understanding. So an example of single genus: intellect if it is assumed that substance is not a genus for it but rather a general accident, and the ten intellects under it are different in reality but each is confined to one individual like the sun. And an example of single species: intellect also if it is assumed that substance is a genus for intellect and substance has no genus, and the ten intellects are its individuals having the same reality. So their existence is not certain; for these two assumptions cannot coexist in reality, otherwise opposites would coexist. (Ismail) Then he said: Definition of the differentia about sharing in the genus: but if you hesitate whether it is a man or a horse or something else, you say: what animal is this? It is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from its partners in animality. If you know this, we say: When we say 'Man, what thing is he in his essence?' the question seeks an essential from the essentials of man that distinguishes him from what shares with him in thingness. So it is valid to answer 'rational animal' just as it is valid to answer 'rational'. Thus it follows that the definition occurs in answer to 'what thing is he in his essence', and also it follows that the definition of the differentia would not prevent it from being true of the definition. This is what Imam al-Razi found problematic. (Abd and Ismail) He said: and it follows, but no one said that; rather the definition is answered only when asked about the species by 'what is it?' (Ismail) Also as it follows that the complete definition occurs in answer to 'what thing', it is correct that it does not occur in answer to 'what thing' but occurs in answer to 'what is the definition'. For the composite 'rational animal' is a definition, then it would be true of it that it is said of the thing in answer to 'what thing is he in his essence' while the definition is not a differentia; because it is composed of differentia and genus, and the composite of a thing and something else is other than that thing. Also the five universals are a division of the simple universal, not the composite, and the definition is composite, outside the five. So here are two problems: confusion and that the definition of differentia does not exclude the definition. (Abd) He found it problematic. And it is appropriate to formulate the problem as: what is sought by 'what thing is he in his essence'? If it is what distinguishes with complete distinction, then the remote differentia would be excluded from the definition of differentia; and if what distinguishes in some respect, then the definition would apply to genus and complete definition. To this points his statement: 'and by this the definition and genus are excluded'. And the answer to this formulation of the problem is that what is meant by distinction is essential distinction in some respect. So what is meant is that 'what thing' seeks the simple that distinguishes essentially in some respect, and on this estimate the differentia is determined in answer to 'what thing is he' and nothing else; for the simple that distinguishes essentially is nothing but the differentia. As for the genus, it does not distinguish the essence except through the proximate differentia, and its proximate differentia is a remote differentia. So the real distinguisher is the differentia of the essence. So when we say 'Man, what thing is he in his substance?' nothing falls in the answer except 'rational'; for it distinguishes essentially without any other thing, unlike 'animal'; for although it distinguishes from inanimates and plants, it does so not essentially but through the differentia of man, even if remote, which is the growing and sentient. And the definition, although it is not simple, distinguishes through the differentia as well. (Ismail)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage defines the third of the five universals: the differentia (fasl). The author begins by stating that the differentia is what is said of a thing in answer to 'what thing is it in its essence' — provided that it distinguishes that thing. This is the core definition. The subsequent discussion addresses several related issues. First, the passage explains the intermediate levels between high and low species and genera. It notes that between the highest genus (genus summum) and the lowest species (species infima) there are intermediate genera and species. For example, 'body' is an intermediate genus because it has a genus above it (substance) and a genus below it (growing body). 'Animal' is an intermediate species because it has a species above it (growing body) and a species below it (man). The author then explains why the text's author (the matn author) did not discuss the 'single genus' (jins mufrad) and 'single species' (naw' mufrad) — these are not part of the hierarchical chain because a single genus has no genus above it and a single species has no species below it. The passage provides hypothetical examples (like intellect assuming certain conditions) but notes that such pure cases are not certain to exist in reality. The main philosophical problem arises when we apply the definition of differentia to the complete definition (hadd) and the genus. If we ask 'what thing is man in his essence?' the answer could be 'rational animal' (the complete definition) or just 'rational' (the differentia). This would mean that the definition of differentia also applies to the definition, which is not a differentia. Imam al-Razi raised this objection. The resolution offered is that the question 'what thing' seeks a simple essential distinguisher in some respect, which is exclusively the differentia. The genus does not distinguish the essence except through the differentia, and the definition distinguishes through its parts. Thus, properly understood, the differentia is the only simple term that answers the question 'what thing is it in its essence' directly without intermediary. The passage concludes by clarifying that 'animal' distinguishes from other categories but only through the differentia of man (e.g., sentient, growing), so it is not a direct essential distinguisher.

Key Terms
الفصل
الحد
الجنس
النوع
الجنس المفرد
النوع المفرد

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the genus 'animal' not qualify as a differentia for man?
A) Because 'animal' does not distinguish man from non-animals
B) Because 'animal' distinguishes man only through an intermediate differentia (e.g., sentient, growing)
C) Because 'animal' is not a simple term
D) Because 'animal' is not one of the five universals

Key Takeaway
The differentia is the only simple universal that directly and essentially distinguishes a thing in answer to 'what thing is it in its essence', excluding the complete definition and the genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the differentia in the definition of 'salat' (prayer) in Islamic law: 'Salat is an act of worship consisting of specific words and actions, beginning with takbir and ending with taslim, with intention.' Write down which part is the genus and which part is the differentia. Explain why the differentia alone answers 'what thing is salat in its essence?'
?
Consider the objection: 'But the complete definition of salat also answers what thing it is.' Using the resolution from this passage, argue why only the differentia (the specific words and actions) is the simple essential distinguisher.

The Definition of the Differentia (al-Fasl) and Its Role in Defining Species
Author defines differentia, raises and resolves issues with its definition applying to complete definition and genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the differentia in a definition and distinguish it from the genus and complete definition.

Core Idea
The differentia is the essential distinguisher within the genus, but its definition risks applying to the whole definition.

The differentia (al-fasl) is a fundamental concept in the five universals. It is what answers the question 'What is it in its essence?' for a species after the genus is known. In this passage, the author defines the differentia and immediately confronts a critical problem: that this definition seems to also fit the complete definition and the genus. This lesson will help you understand the differentia's precise role and why it must be carefully distinguished.

Guided Path
1
Locate the standard definition of the differentia
Find the sentence: 'هو المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته'. This is the definiendum.
2
Apply the definition to a concrete example: man
When asked 'What is man in his essence?', possible answers are 'rational animal' (complete definition) and 'rational' (differentia). Both seem to satisfy the definition.
3
Identify the genus and differentia in the definition of man
Genus = 'animal', differentia = 'rational'. The differentia alone distinguishes man from other animals.
4
Recognize the overlap problem
The definition of differentia also applies to 'rational animal', meaning it is not exclusive. This is the problem Imam al-Razi raised.

تعريف الفصل: هو المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، لكن ترددت في أنه هل هو إنسان أو فرس أو غيرهما، تقول: أي حيوان هذا؟ فيجاب بما يخصصه ويميزه عن مشاركاته في الحيوانية. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: إذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في ذاته" كان المطلوب ذاتيا من ذاتيات الإنسان يميزه عما يشاركه في الشيئية، فيصح أن يجاب بأنه حيوان ناطق، كما يصح أن يجاب بأنه ناطق، فيلزم صحة وقوع الحد في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، وأيضا يلزم أن لا يكون تعريف الفصل مانعا لصدقه على الحد، وهذا مما استشكله الإمام الرازي. فیلزم ولم يقل به أحد بل إنما يجاب بالحد إذا سئل عن النوع بما هو. وأيضًا كما يلزم وقوع الحد التام في جواب أي شيء صح أنه لا يقع في جواب أي شيء بل يقع في جواب ما الحد فإن مجموع الحيوان الناطق حد يصدق حينئذ عليه أنه المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته مع أن الحد ليس بفصل؛ لأنه مركب من الفصل والجنس والمركب من الشيء وغيره مغاير لذلك الشيء، وأيضا الكليات الخمسة قسم للكلي المفرد لا المركب والحد مركب خارج عن الخمسة، فههنا إشكالان: الخلط وعدم مانعة تعريف الفصل بالحد. وينبغي تقرير الإشكال بأن المطلوب من أي شيء هو في ذاته إن كان ما يميز تميزا تاما يخرج الفصل البعيد عن تعريف الفصل، وإن كان ما يميز تميزا في الجملة فيصدق التعريف على الجنس والحد التام. وإلى هذا يشير قوله وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس والجواب على هذا التقرير عن هذا الإشكال أن المراد من الامتياز الامتياز بالذات في الجملة، فالمراد أن أي شيء يطلب المفرد المميز بالذات في الجملة وعلى هذا التقدير تعين الفصل في جواب أي شيء هو لا غير؛ فإن المفرد المميز بالذات ليس إلا الفصل، وأما الجنس فليس مميزا للماهية إلا بواسطة الفصل القريب، وفصله القريب فصل بعيد، فالمميز في الحقيقة فصل الماهية فإذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في جوهره؟" فلا يقع في الجواب إلا الناطق؛ فإنه مميز بالذات لا بواسطة شيء آخر بخلاف الحيوان؛ فإنه وإن كان مميزا عن الجمادات والنباتات لكنه لا بالذات بل بواسطة فصل الإنسان وإن كان بعيدا هو النامي والحساس والحد مع أنه ليس بمفرد يميز بواسطة الفصل أيضًا. في هذا المقام، وأجاب صاحب المحاكمات بأن معنى "أي" وإن كان بحسب اللغة طلب المميز مطلقا لكن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا على أنه يطلب به مميز لا يكون مقولا في جواب ما هو، وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس أيضًا، وللمحقق الطوسي ههنا مسلك آخر أدق وأتقن وهو إنا لا نسأل عن الفصل إلا بعد أن نعلم أن للشيء جنسا؛ بناء على أن ما لا جنس له لا فصل له، وإذا علمنا الشيء بالجنس فنطلب ما يميزه عن مشاركاته في ذلك الجنس، فنقول: الإنسان أي حيوان هو في ذاته؟ فتعين الجواب بالناطق لا غير. فكلمته "شيء" صاحب المحاكمات يعني مولانا قطب الدين الرازي يطلب به حاصل الجواب: اختيار الشق الثاني يعني أن المراد ما يميز تميزا في الجملة لكن لا مطلقا بل المراد المميز الذي لا يكون مقولا في جواب ما هو الحد التام ليس بمقول في جواب ما هو إلا إذا سئل عن الأمر الكلي والجنس إذا سئل عن مختلفة الحقائق والتمييز كل واحد منهما في الجملة يقالان في جواب ما هو ما يقال في جواب ما هو لا يقال في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته بحسب اصطلاح أرباب العقول وصحة وقوعها في جواب أي شيء بحسب اللغة لا يضرنا؛ لأن كلامنا في مصطلحهم. آخر في دفع الإشكال المذكور. أدق لأن فيه ملاحظة معنى الفصل وحال السائل الطالب به بأنه علم الجنس أولا ثم يطلب فصلا. وأتقن السلامة عن الطعن الذي في جواب العلامة الرازي لله، وهو أن الجواب بأن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا هكذا ولا مشاحة في الاصطلاح جواب على رسم أرباب المعقول. بالناطق لأن الجنس قد علم فلا حاجة إلى الجواب به فقط ولا بانضمامه إلى الناطق. فإن قلت: إن الناطق بمعنى مدرك الكليات ليس مختصا بالإنسان؛ لأن الباري عز شأنه وسائر المجردات كالعقول والنفوس الفلكية يدركون الكليات أيضاً، فلا يصح كونه فصلا قريبا للإنسان؛ لما تقرر عندهم أن الفصل القريب لابد أن يكون مختصاً بالماهية التي هو فصل لها، ولو سلم أن الفصل القريب لا يجب أن يكون مختصا بتلك الماهية فجعله فصلا للإنسان ليس أولى من جعله جنسا له بل يجوز أن يجعل الحيوان فصلا أو الناطق جنسا؛ فإن كل واحد منهما مشترك بين ماهية الإنسان وغيرها قلت المراد من الناطق هو صاحب مبدأ النطق والإدراك، ولا شك أن ذلك المبدأ مختص بماهية الإنسان الذي هو أثر ذلك المبدأ فلا إشكال.
Definition of the differentia: It is what is predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?', but you hesitated as to whether it is a man or a horse or other than them. You say: 'Which animal is this?' So it is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from its partners in animality. If you know this, we say: When we say 'Man, what is he in his essence?' the sought is an essential from the essentials of man that distinguishes him from what shares with him in thingness. So it is valid to answer with 'rational animal', just as it is valid to answer with 'rational'. So it follows the validity of the complete definition falling under the answer to 'What is it in its essence?', and also it follows that the definition of the differentia is not exclusive, for it applies to the complete definition. This is what Imam al-Razi considered problematic. He said: 'It follows, and no one has said it; rather the complete definition is answered only when asked about the species in terms of what it is.' Also, just as it follows that the complete definition falls under the answer to 'What is it?' it is correct that it does not fall under the answer to 'What is it?' rather it falls under the answer to 'What is the definition?' For the totality of 'rational animal' is a complete definition that at that point is true of being predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?' while the complete definition is not a differentia because it is composed of differentia and genus, and the composite of a thing and other than it is other than that thing. Also, the five universals are a division of the single universal, not the composite, and the complete definition is composite and outside the five. So here are two problems: confusion and lack of exclusivity of the definition of differentia with respect to the complete definition. And the problem should be formulated as follows: The sought from 'What is it in its essence?' – if it is what distinguishes completely, the distant differentia would be excluded from the definition of differentia; and if it is what distinguishes partially, then the definition applies to the genus and the complete definition. And to this his statement points: 'And by this the complete definition and the genus are excluded.' And the answer according to this formulation to this problem is that what is meant by distinction is essential distinction in part. So the meaning is that 'What is it?' seeks the single thing that distinguishes essentially in part. On this basis, the differentia is determined in the answer to 'What is it?' and nothing else. For the single thing that distinguishes essentially is nothing but the differentia. As for the genus, it does not distinguish the quiddity except through the proximate differentia, and its proximate differentia is a distant differentia. So the real distinguisher is the differentia of the quiddity. So when we say 'Man, what is he in his substance?' nothing falls in the answer except 'rational', for it distinguishes essentially without any intermediary, contrary to 'animal'; for although it distinguishes from inanimates and plants, it does not do so essentially but through the differentia of man, even if distant, which is 'growing' and 'sentient'. And the complete definition, even though it is not single, distinguishes through the differentia as well. At this point, the author of al-Muhakamat answered: The meaning of 'ayy' (which) in language is the request for a distinguisher absolutely, but the people of rational discourse have stipulated that by it is sought a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' And by this the complete definition and the genus are also excluded. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi has here another approach that is more subtle and more precise: that we do not ask about the differentia except after we know that the thing has a genus, based on the fact that what has no genus has no differentia. And when we know the thing by its genus, we seek what distinguishes it from its partners in that genus. So we say: 'Man, which animal is he in his essence?' Then the answer is determined as 'rational' and nothing else. His word 'thing' – the author of al-Muhakamat, meaning our master Qutb al-Din al-Razi, seeks by it the content of the answer: choosing the second side means that what is meant is what distinguishes partially, but not absolutely; rather what is meant is the distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' The complete definition is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' except when asked about the universal matter; and the genus, when asked about different realities, and each of them partially are said in answer to 'What is it?' – what is said in answer to 'What is it?' is not said in answer to 'Which thing is it in its essence?' according to the convention of the people of rational discourse. And the validity of their falling under the answer to 'Which thing?' according to language does not harm us because our speech is in their terminology. Another [response] in repelling the mentioned problem. More subtle because it observes the meaning of the differentia and the state of the questioner seeking it, that he knows the genus first then seeks a differentia. And more precise due to safety from the criticism directed at the response of 'Allama al-Razi – may God have mercy on him – which is that the answer 'the people of rational discourse stipulated thus, and there is no quarrel over terminology' is a response in the manner of the people of rational discourse. [He answered] with 'rational' because the genus is already known, so there is no need to answer with it alone nor with its combination with 'rational'. If you say: 'Rational' meaning 'apprehender of universals' is not specific to man because the Exalted Creator and other abstract entities like intellects and celestial souls also apprehend universals, so it cannot be a proximate differentia for man because they have established that the proximate differentia must be specific to the quiddity for which it is a differentia. And even if conceded that the proximate differentia does not have to be specific to that quiddity, then making it a differentia for man is no more suitable than making it a genus for him. Rather it is possible to make 'animal' a differentia or 'rational' a genus, for each of them is shared between the quiddity of man and others. I say: What is meant by 'rational' is the possessor of the principle of speech and perception, and there is no doubt that that principle is specific to the quiddity of man who is the effect of that principle, so there is no problem.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines the differentia (al-fasl) and addresses the problem that its definition might also apply to the complete definition (al-hadd al-tamm) and the genus. The author begins by stating the standard definition: the differentia is what is predicated in answer to 'What is it in its essence?' This distinguishes the species from others sharing the same genus. However, if one asks about man 'What is he in his essence?', one could answer 'rational animal' (the complete definition) or just 'rational' (the differentia). This causes two problems: (1) the complete definition would then fall under the definition of differentia, but it is not a differentia because it is composite; (2) the definition of differentia is not exclusive since it applies to the complete definition. The author then clarifies that the sought distinction is essential but partial, so only the differentia (a single term) truly distinguishes essentially, while the genus and complete definition distinguish only through the differentia. Two solutions are presented: from the author of al-Muhakamat (Qutb al-Din al-Razi), who argues that in logical terminology 'ayy' seeks a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?', thus excluding the genus and complete definition; and from al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi, who argues that we first know the genus and then ask for the differentia within that genus (e.g., 'Which animal is man?'), so the answer is only the differentia. The passage ends by addressing an objection: 'rational' might not be specific to man because God and celestial beings also apprehend universals. The response is that 'rational' here means 'possessor of the principle of speech and perception', which is unique to humans.

Key Terms
الفصل
الحد
الجنس
الناطق

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can 'rational' be the differentia of man even though God and angels also apprehend universals?
A) Because 'rational' means 'possessor of the principle of speech and perception', which is unique to humans.
B) Because the differentia does not need to be exclusive.
C) Because God and angels are not considered in logic.
D) Because 'rational' in this context means 'mortal'.

Key Takeaway
The differentia is the single term that essentially distinguishes a species within its genus, but its definition must be carefully limited to avoid encompassing the complete definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the definition of 'wine' as 'an intoxicating drink made from grapes', identify the genus and differentia, and explain whether 'intoxicating' could serve as a differentia for all alcoholic beverages in fiqh.

The Problem of Overlap: Why the Differentia's Definition Applies to the Complete Definition and Genus
Author defines differentia, raises and resolves issues with its definition applying to complete definition and genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Imam al-Razi's objection that the definition of differentia is not exclusive.

Core Idea
Imam al-Razi revealed a flaw: the definition of differentia equally fits the complete definition, which is composite and not a differentia.

After defining the differentia, the author confronts a serious objection attributed to Imam al-Razi. If the differentia is 'what is predicated in answer to What is it in its essence?', then the complete definition 'rational animal' also qualifies. This would make the differentia's definition non-exclusive and create confusion between a simple term and a composite. This lesson examines the precise formulation of the problem.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of the differentia
Recall: 'هو المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته'.
2
Test the definition on the complete definition of man
Take 'حد الإنسان: حيوان ناطق'. Ask: does 'حيوان ناطق' satisfy the definition? It is predicated of man in answer to 'What is he in his essence?'.
3
Observe the consequence
If true, then the complete definition (a composite) would be considered a differentia, which is impossible because a differentia is a single universal.
4
Formulate the two problems
(1) The definition of differentia does not exclude the complete definition (lack of exclusivity). (2) The complete definition, though composite, would be called a differentia (confusion).
5
Note the implication for the genus as well
The definition also applies to the genus 'animal' when asked about man, since 'animal' distinguishes man from plants and minerals, though not essentially.

الجملة يقالان في جواب ما هو ما يقال في جواب ما هو لا يقال في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته بحسب اصطلاح أرباب العقول وصحة وقوعها في جواب أي شيء بحسب اللغة لا يضرنا؛ لأن كلامنا في مصطلحهم. آخر في دفع الإشكال المذكور. أدق لأن فيه ملاحظة معنى الفصل وحال السائل الطالب به بأنه علم الجنس أولا ثم يطلب فصلا. وأتقن السلامة عن الطعن الذي في جواب العلامة الرازي لله، وهو أن الجواب بأن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا هكذا ولا مشاحة في الاصطلاح جواب على رسم أرباب المعقول. بالناطق لأن الجنس قد علم فلا حاجة إلى الجواب به فقط ولا بانضمامه إلى الناطق. فإن قلت: إن الناطق بمعنى مدرك الكليات ليس مختصا بالإنسان؛ لأن الباري عز شأنه وسائر المجردات كالعقول والنفوس الفلكية يدركون الكليات أيضاً، فلا يصح كونه فصلا قريبا للإنسان؛ لما تقرر عندهم أن الفصل القريب لابد أن يكون مختصاً بالماهية التي هو فصل لها، ولو سلم أن الفصل القريب لا يجب أن يكون مختصا بتلك الماهية فجعله فصلا للإنسان ليس أولى من جعله جنسا له بل يجوز أن يجعل الحيوان فصلا أو الناطق جنسا؛ فإن كل واحد منهما مشترك بين ماهية الإنسان وغيرها قلت المراد من الناطق هو صاحب مبدأ النطق والإدراك، ولا شك أن ذلك المبدأ مختص بماهية الإنسان الذي هو أثر ذلك المبدأ فلا إشكال.
Definition of the differentia: It is what is predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?', but you hesitated as to whether it is a man or a horse or other than them. You say: 'Which animal is this?' So it is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from its partners in animality. If you know this, we say: When we say 'Man, what is he in his essence?' the sought is an essential from the essentials of man that distinguishes him from what shares with him in thingness. So it is valid to answer with 'rational animal', just as it is valid to answer with 'rational'. So it follows the validity of the complete definition falling under the answer to 'What is it in its essence?', and also it follows that the definition of the differentia is not exclusive, for it applies to the complete definition. This is what Imam al-Razi considered problematic. He said: 'It follows, and no one has said it; rather the complete definition is answered only when asked about the species in terms of what it is.' Also, just as it follows that the complete definition falls under the answer to 'What is it?' it is correct that it does not fall under the answer to 'What is it?' rather it falls under the answer to 'What is the definition?' For the totality of 'rational animal' is a complete definition that at that point is true of being predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?' while the complete definition is not a differentia because it is composed of differentia and genus, and the composite of a thing and other than it is other than that thing. Also, the five universals are a division of the single universal, not the composite, and the complete definition is composite and outside the five. So here are two problems: confusion and lack of exclusivity of the definition of differentia with respect to the complete definition. And the problem should be formulated as follows: The sought from 'What is it in its essence?' – if it is what distinguishes completely, the distant differentia would be excluded from the definition of differentia; and if it is what distinguishes partially, then the definition applies to the genus and the complete definition. And to this his statement points: 'And by this the complete definition and the genus are excluded.' And the answer according to this formulation to this problem is that what is meant by distinction is essential distinction in part. So the meaning is that 'What is it?' seeks the single thing that distinguishes essentially in part. On this basis, the differentia is determined in the answer to 'What is it?' and nothing else. For the single thing that distinguishes essentially is nothing but the differentia. As for the genus, it does not distinguish the quiddity except through the proximate differentia, and its proximate differentia is a distant differentia. So the real distinguisher is the differentia of the quiddity. So when we say 'Man, what is he in his substance?' nothing falls in the answer except 'rational', for it distinguishes essentially without any intermediary, contrary to 'animal'; for although it distinguishes from inanimates and plants, it does not do so essentially but through the differentia of man, even if distant, which is 'growing' and 'sentient'. And the complete definition, even though it is not single, distinguishes through the differentia as well. At this point, the author of al-Muhakamat answered: The meaning of 'ayy' (which) in language is the request for a distinguisher absolutely, but the people of rational discourse have stipulated that by it is sought a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' And by this the complete definition and the genus are also excluded. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi has here another approach that is more subtle and more precise: that we do not ask about the differentia except after we know that the thing has a genus, based on the fact that what has no genus has no differentia. And when we know the thing by its genus, we seek what distinguishes it from its partners in that genus. So we say: 'Man, which animal is he in his essence?' Then the answer is determined as 'rational' and nothing else. His word 'thing' – the author of al-Muhakamat, meaning our master Qutb al-Din al-Razi, seeks by it the content of the answer: choosing the second side means that what is meant is what distinguishes partially, but not absolutely; rather what is meant is the distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' The complete definition is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' except when asked about the universal matter; and the genus, when asked about different realities, and each of them partially are said in answer to 'What is it?' – what is said in answer to 'What is it?' is not said in answer to 'Which thing is it in its essence?' according to the convention of the people of rational discourse. And the validity of their falling under the answer to 'Which thing?' according to language does not harm us because our speech is in their terminology. Another [response] in repelling the mentioned problem. More subtle because it observes the meaning of the differentia and the state of the questioner seeking it, that he knows the genus first then seeks a differentia. And more precise due to safety from the criticism directed at the response of 'Allama al-Razi – may God have mercy on him – which is that the answer 'the people of rational discourse stipulated thus, and there is no quarrel over terminology' is a response in the manner of the people of rational discourse. [He answered] with 'rational' because the genus is already known, so there is no need to answer with it alone nor with its combination with 'rational'. If you say: 'Rational' meaning 'apprehender of universals' is not specific to man because the Exalted Creator and other abstract entities like intellects and celestial souls also apprehend universals, so it cannot be a proximate differentia for man because they have established that the proximate differentia must be specific to the quiddity for which it is a differentia. And even if conceded that the proximate differentia does not have to be specific to that quiddity, then making it a differentia for man is no more suitable than making it a genus for him. Rather it is possible to make 'animal' a differentia or 'rational' a genus, for each of them is shared between the quiddity of man and others. I say: What is meant by 'rational' is the possessor of the principle of speech and perception, and there is no doubt that that principle is specific to the quiddity of man who is the effect of that principle, so there is no problem.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines the differentia (al-fasl) and addresses the problem that its definition might also apply to the complete definition (al-hadd al-tamm) and the genus. The author begins by stating the standard definition: the differentia is what is predicated in answer to 'What is it in its essence?' This distinguishes the species from others sharing the same genus. However, if one asks about man 'What is he in his essence?', one could answer 'rational animal' (the complete definition) or just 'rational' (the differentia). This causes two problems: (1) the complete definition would then fall under the definition of differentia, but it is not a differentia because it is composite; (2) the definition of differentia is not exclusive since it applies to the complete definition. The author then clarifies that the sought distinction is essential but partial, so only the differentia (a single term) truly distinguishes essentially, while the genus and complete definition distinguish only through the differentia. Two solutions are presented: from the author of al-Muhakamat (Qutb al-Din al-Razi), who argues that in logical terminology 'ayy' seeks a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?', thus excluding the genus and complete definition; and from al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi, who argues that we first know the genus and then ask for the differentia within that genus (e.g., 'Which animal is man?'), so the answer is only the differentia. The passage ends by addressing an objection: 'rational' might not be specific to man because God and celestial beings also apprehend universals. The response is that 'rational' here means 'possessor of the principle of speech and perception', which is unique to humans.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Imam al-Razi consider problematic about the definition of differentia?
A) It is too narrow.
B) It applies to the complete definition.
C) It is linguistically incorrect.
D) It is not found in Aristotle.

Key Takeaway
The definition of differentia must be exclusive to the differentia alone; applying it to the complete definition is a logical error that the tradition resolves through careful specification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'prohibition (haram)' in usul al-fiqh: 'a demand to abstain with firmness'. Test whether this definition also applies to 'obligation (wajib)' if only the wording changes. Identify where the exclusivity fails.

The Five Universals
intermediate
10 min
Resolving the Overlap: The Partial Distinction Solution
Author defines differentia, raises and resolves issues with its definition applying to complete definition and genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the solution that the differentia distinguishes essentially but partially, excluding the complete definition.

Core Idea
Only the differentia distinguishes essentially and by itself; the genus and complete definition distinguish only through the differentia.

The author provides a direct answer to the overlap problem. He clarifies that the definition of differentia should be understood as seeking a partial essential distinction. The differentia alone is a single term that distinguishes the species without any intermediary. The genus and complete definition, by contrast, rely on the differentia to do the distinguishing. This lesson walks through that subtle but crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Recall the formulation of the problem
The definition of differentia seems to fit the complete definition.
2
Understand the key phrase: 'الامتياز بالذات في الجملة' (essential distinction in part)
The differentia is requested as a single term that distinguishes the quiddity essentially, not a composite.
3
Apply to the genus: animal
When asked 'What is man in his essence?', answering 'animal' does provide some distinction, but that distinction is not essential because 'animal' by itself does not specify man; it requires the differentia 'rational' to do so. So animal distinguishes through the differentia, not by itself.
4
Apply to the complete definition: rational animal
It is composite, so it distinguishes through its parts, not as a single term. Therefore, it is not a differentia.
5
Conclude that only the differentia satisfies the definition properly
Thus, the definition is exclusive after all, when interpreted correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف الفصل: هو المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، لكن ترددت في أنه هل هو إنسان أو فرس أو غيرهما، تقول: أي حيوان هذا؟ فيجاب بما يخصصه ويميزه عن مشاركاته في الحيوانية. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: إذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في ذاته" كان المطلوب ذاتيا من ذاتيات الإنسان يميزه عما يشاركه في الشيئية، فيصح أن يجاب بأنه حيوان ناطق، كما يصح أن يجاب بأنه ناطق، فيلزم صحة وقوع الحد في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، وأيضا يلزم أن لا يكون تعريف الفصل مانعا لصدقه على الحد، وهذا مما استشكله الإمام الرازي. فیلزم ولم يقل به أحد بل إنما يجاب بالحد إذا سئل عن النوع بما هو. وأيضًا كما يلزم وقوع الحد التام في جواب أي شيء صح أنه لا يقع في جواب أي شيء بل يقع في جواب ما الحد فإن مجموع الحيوان الناطق حد يصدق حينئذ عليه أنه المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته مع أن الحد ليس بفصل؛ لأنه مركب من الفصل والجنس والمركب من الشيء وغيره مغاير لذلك الشيء، وأيضا الكليات الخمسة قسم للكلي المفرد لا المركب والحد مركب خارج عن الخمسة، فههنا إشكالان: الخلط وعدم مانعة تعريف الفصل بالحد. وينبغي تقرير الإشكال بأن المطلوب من أي شيء هو في ذاته إن كان ما يميز تميزا تاما يخرج الفصل البعيد عن تعريف الفصل، وإن كان ما يميز تميزا في الجملة فيصدق التعريف على الجنس والحد التام. وإلى هذا يشير قوله وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس والجواب على هذا التقرير عن هذا الإشكال أن المراد من الامتياز الامتياز بالذات في الجملة، فالمراد أن أي شيء يطلب المفرد المميز بالذات في الجملة وعلى هذا التقدير تعين الفصل في جواب أي شيء هو لا غير؛ فإن المفرد المميز بالذات ليس إلا الفصل، وأما الجنس فليس مميزا للماهية إلا بواسطة الفصل القريب، وفصله القريب فصل بعيد، فالمميز في الحقيقة فصل الماهية فإذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في جوهره؟" فلا يقع في الجواب إلا الناطق؛ فإنه مميز بالذات لا بواسطة شيء آخر بخلاف الحيوان؛ فإنه وإن كان مميزا عن الجمادات والنباتات لكنه لا بالذات بل بواسطة فصل الإنسان وإن كان بعيدا هو النامي والحساس والحد مع أنه ليس بمفرد يميز بواسطة الفصل أيضًا. في هذا المقام، وأجاب صاحب المحاكمات بأن معنى "أي" وإن كان بحسب اللغة طلب المميز مطلقا لكن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا على أنه يطلب به مميز لا يكون مقولا في جواب ما هو، وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس أيضًا، وللمحقق الطوسي ههنا مسلك آخر أدق وأتقن وهو إنا لا نسأل عن الفصل إلا بعد أن نعلم أن للشيء جنسا؛ بناء على أن ما لا جنس له لا فصل له، وإذا علمنا الشيء بالجنس فنطلب ما يميزه عن مشاركاته في ذلك الجنس، فنقول: الإنسان أي حيوان هو في ذاته؟ فتعين الجواب بالناطق لا غير. فكلمته "شيء" صاحب المحاكمات يعني مولانا قطب الدين الرازي يطلب به حاصل الجواب: اختيار الشق الثاني يعني أن المراد ما يميز تميزا في الجملة لكن لا مطلقا بل المراد المميز الذي لا يكون مقولا في جواب ما هو الحد التام ليس بمقول في جواب ما هو إلا إذا سئل عن الأمر الكلي والجنس إذا سئل عن مختلفة الحقائق والتمييز كل واحد منهما في الجملة يقالان في جواب ما هو ما يقال في جواب ما هو لا يقال في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته بحسب اصطلاح أرباب العقول وصحة وقوعها في جواب أي شيء بحسب اللغة لا يضرنا؛ لأن كلامنا في مصطلحهم. آخر في دفع الإشكال المذكور. أدق لأن فيه ملاحظة معنى الفصل وحال السائل الطالب به بأنه علم الجنس أولا ثم يطلب فصلا. وأتقن السلامة عن الطعن الذي في جواب العلامة الرازي لله، وهو أن الجواب بأن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا هكذا ولا مشاحة في الاصطلاح جواب على رسم أرباب المعقول. بالناطق لأن الجنس قد علم فلا حاجة إلى الجواب به فقط ولا بانضمامه إلى الناطق. فإن قلت: إن الناطق بمعنى مدرك الكليات ليس مختصا بالإنسان؛ لأن الباري عز شأنه Definition of the differentia: It is what is predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?', but you hesitated as to whether it is a man or a horse or other than them. You say: 'Which animal is this?' So it is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from its partners in animality. Commentary

Checkpoint
According to the partial distinction solution, why does the genus 'animal' not count as a differentia for man?
A) Because it is not predicated essentially.
B) Because it distinguishes only through the differentia.
C) Because it is composite.

Key Takeaway
The differentia's definition must be understood as seeking a single essential distinguisher, which excludes both the genus and the composite definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition of 'salat' as 'specific actions and sayings beginning with takbir and ending with taslim'. Identify which part is the genus and which is the differentia. Then argue why the complete definition is not itself a differentia.

The Five Universals
intermediate
10 min
Alternative Resolutions: Qutb al-Din al-Razi's Stipulation and al-Tusi's Epistemic Order
Author defines differentia, raises and resolves issues with its definition applying to complete definition and genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the two additional solutions to the differentia's definition problem: the terminological stipulation and the epistemic order.

Core Idea
Two master logicians offered elegant solutions: one by redefining the question term, another by sequencing the knowledge of genus before seeking differentia.

In addition to the author's own solution, two other eminent scholars—Qutb al-Din al-Razi and Nasir al-Din al-Tusi—provided alternative resolutions to the overlap problem. Qutb al-Din proposed that in logical terminology, the word 'ayy' (which) specifically seeks a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' (the genus question). Al-Tusi, more subtly, argued that one asks for a differentia only after already knowing the genus, so the answer is naturally narrowed to the differentia alone. This lesson analyzes both approaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify Qutb al-Din's claim
The logical term 'ayy' has a stipulated meaning: it asks for a distinguisher that is not also a predicate answering 'What is it?' (the genus question).
2
Apply to the complete definition
The complete definition 'rational animal' does answer 'What is man?' (the genus question). Therefore, it is excluded from answering 'Which thing?' according to this stipulation.
3
Assess this solution
It is effective but relies on terminological convention; it may be seen as avoiding the issue rather than explaining the underlying logic.
4
Understand al-Tusi's approach
He observes that we first know the thing by its genus (e.g., man is an animal). Then we ask 'Which animal is he in his essence?' This already presupposes the genus, so the answer can only be the differentia (rational), not the genus again or the composite.
5
Evaluate the superiority
Al-Tusi's method is more robust because it reflects the natural epistemic process and avoids the need for stipulation. The author praises it as more subtle and precise.

تعريف الفصل: هو المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، لكن ترددت في أنه هل هو إنسان أو فرس أو غيرهما، تقول: أي حيوان هذا؟ فيجاب بما يخصصه ويميزه عن مشاركاته في الحيوانية. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: إذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في ذاته" كان المطلوب ذاتيا من ذاتيات الإنسان يميزه عما يشاركه في الشيئية، فيصح أن يجاب بأنه حيوان ناطق، كما يصح أن يجاب بأنه ناطق، فيلزم صحة وقوع الحد في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته، وأيضا يلزم أن لا يكون تعريف الفصل مانعا لصدقه على الحد، وهذا مما استشكله الإمام الرازي. فیلزم ولم يقل به أحد بل إنما يجاب بالحد إذا سئل عن النوع بما هو. وأيضًا كما يلزم وقوع الحد التام في جواب أي شيء صح أنه لا يقع في جواب أي شيء بل يقع في جواب ما الحد فإن مجموع الحيوان الناطق حد يصدق حينئذ عليه أنه المقول على الشيء في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته مع أن الحد ليس بفصل؛ لأنه مركب من الفصل والجنس والمركب من الشيء وغيره مغاير لذلك الشيء، وأيضا الكليات الخمسة قسم للكلي المفرد لا المركب والحد مركب خارج عن الخمسة، فههنا إشكالان: الخلط وعدم مانعة تعريف الفصل بالحد. وينبغي تقرير الإشكال بأن المطلوب من أي شيء هو في ذاته إن كان ما يميز تميزا تاما يخرج الفصل البعيد عن تعريف الفصل، وإن كان ما يميز تميزا في الجملة فيصدق التعريف على الجنس والحد التام. وإلى هذا يشير قوله وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس والجواب على هذا التقرير عن هذا الإشكال أن المراد من الامتياز الامتياز بالذات في الجملة، فالمراد أن أي شيء يطلب المفرد المميز بالذات في الجملة وعلى هذا التقدير تعين الفصل في جواب أي شيء هو لا غير؛ فإن المفرد المميز بالذات ليس إلا الفصل، وأما الجنس فليس مميزا للماهية إلا بواسطة الفصل القريب، وفصله القريب فصل بعيد، فالمميز في الحقيقة فصل الماهية فإذا قلنا: "الإنسان أي شيء هو في جوهره؟" فلا يقع في الجواب إلا الناطق؛ فإنه مميز بالذات لا بواسطة شيء آخر بخلاف الحيوان؛ فإنه وإن كان مميزا عن الجمادات والنباتات لكنه لا بالذات بل بواسطة فصل الإنسان وإن كان بعيدا هو النامي والحساس والحد مع أنه ليس بمفرد يميز بواسطة الفصل أيضًا. في هذا المقام، وأجاب صاحب المحاكمات بأن معنى "أي" وإن كان بحسب اللغة طلب المميز مطلقا لكن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا على أنه يطلب به مميز لا يكون مقولا في جواب ما هو، وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس أيضًا، وللمحقق الطوسي ههنا مسلك آخر أدق وأتقن وهو إنا لا نسأل عن الفصل إلا بعد أن نعلم أن للشيء جنسا؛ بناء على أن ما لا جنس له لا فصل له، وإذا علمنا الشيء بالجنس فنطلب ما يميزه عن مشاركاته في ذلك الجنس، فنقول: الإنسان أي حيوان هو في ذاته؟ فتعين الجواب بالناطق لا غير. فكلمته "شيء" صاحب المحاكمات يعني مولانا قطب الدين الرازي يطلب به حاصل الجواب: اختيار الشق الثاني يعني أن المراد ما يميز تميزا في الجملة لكن لا مطلقا بل المراد المميز الذي لا يكون مقولا في جواب ما هو الحد التام ليس بمقول في جواب ما هو إلا إذا سئل عن الأمر الكلي والجنس إذا سئل عن مختلفة الحقائق والتمييز كل واحد منهما في الجملة يقالان في جواب ما هو ما يقال في جواب ما هو لا يقال في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته بحسب اصطلاح أرباب العقول وصحة وقوعها في جواب أي شيء بحسب اللغة لا يضرنا؛ لأن كلامنا في مصطلحهم. آخر في دفع الإشكال المذكور. أدق لأن فيه ملاحظة معنى الفصل وحال السائل الطالب به بأنه علم الجنس أولا ثم يطلب فصلا. وأتقن السلامة عن الطعن الذي في جواب العلامة الرازي لله، وهو أن الجواب بأن أرباب المعقول اصطلحوا هكذا ولا مشاحة في الاصطلاح جواب على رسم أرباب المعقول. بالناطق لأن الجنس قد علم فلا حاجة إلى الجواب به فقط ولا بانضمامه إلى الناطق. فإن قلت: إن الناطق بمعنى مدرك الكليات ليس مختصا بالإنسان؛ لأن الباري عز شأنه وسائر المجردات كالعقول والنفوس الفلكية يدركون الكليات أيضاً، فلا يصح كونه فصلا قريبا للإنسان؛ لما تقرر عندهم أن الفصل القريب لابد أن يكون مختصاً بالماهية التي هو فصل لها، ولو سلم أن الفصل القريب لا يجب أن يكون مختصا بتلك الماهية فجعله فصلا للإنسان ليس أولى من جعله جنسا له بل يجوز أن يجعل الحيوان فصلا أو الناطق جنسا؛ فإن كل واحد منهما مشترك بين ماهية الإنسان وغيرها قلت المراد من الناطق هو صاحب مبدأ النطق والإدراك، ولا شك أن ذلك المبدأ مختص بماهية الإنسان الذي هو أثر ذلك المبدأ فلا إشكال.
Definition of the differentia: It is what is predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?', but you hesitated as to whether it is a man or a horse or other than them. You say: 'Which animal is this?' So it is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from its partners in animality. If you know this, we say: When we say 'Man, what is he in his essence?' the sought is an essential from the essentials of man that distinguishes him from what shares with him in thingness. So it is valid to answer with 'rational animal', just as it is valid to answer with 'rational'. So it follows the validity of the complete definition falling under the answer to 'What is it in its essence?', and also it follows that the definition of the differentia is not exclusive, for it applies to the complete definition. This is what Imam al-Razi considered problematic. He said: 'It follows, and no one has said it; rather the complete definition is answered only when asked about the species in terms of what it is.' Also, just as it follows that the complete definition falls under the answer to 'What is it?' it is correct that it does not fall under the answer to 'What is it?' rather it falls under the answer to 'What is the definition?' For the totality of 'rational animal' is a complete definition that at that point is true of being predicated of a thing in answer to 'What is it in its essence?' while the complete definition is not a differentia because it is composed of differentia and genus, and the composite of a thing and other than it is other than that thing. Also, the five universals are a division of the single universal, not the composite, and the complete definition is composite and outside the five. So here are two problems: confusion and lack of exclusivity of the definition of differentia with respect to the complete definition. And the problem should be formulated as follows: The sought from 'What is it in its essence?' – if it is what distinguishes completely, the distant differentia would be excluded from the definition of differentia; and if it is what distinguishes partially, then the definition applies to the genus and the complete definition. And to this his statement points: 'And by this the complete definition and the genus are excluded.' And the answer according to this formulation to this problem is that what is meant by distinction is essential distinction in part. So the meaning is that 'What is it?' seeks the single thing that distinguishes essentially in part. On this basis, the differentia is determined in the answer to 'What is it?' and nothing else. For the single thing that distinguishes essentially is nothing but the differentia. As for the genus, it does not distinguish the quiddity except through the proximate differentia, and its proximate differentia is a distant differentia. So the real distinguisher is the differentia of the quiddity. So when we say 'Man, what is he in his substance?' nothing falls in the answer except 'rational', for it distinguishes essentially without any intermediary, contrary to 'animal'; for although it distinguishes from inanimates and plants, it does not do so essentially but through the differentia of man, even if distant, which is 'growing' and 'sentient'. And the complete definition, even though it is not single, distinguishes through the differentia as well. At this point, the author of al-Muhakamat answered: The meaning of 'ayy' (which) in language is the request for a distinguisher absolutely, but the people of rational discourse have stipulated that by it is sought a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' And by this the complete definition and the genus are also excluded. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi has here another approach that is more subtle and more precise: that we do not ask about the differentia except after we know that the thing has a genus, based on the fact that what has no genus has no differentia. And when we know the thing by its genus, we seek what distinguishes it from its partners in that genus. So we say: 'Man, which animal is he in his essence?' Then the answer is determined as 'rational' and nothing else. His word 'thing' – the author of al-Muhakamat, meaning our master Qutb al-Din al-Razi, seeks by it the content of the answer: choosing the second side means that what is meant is what distinguishes partially, but not absolutely; rather what is meant is the distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' The complete definition is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?' except when asked about the universal matter; and the genus, when asked about different realities, and each of them partially are said in answer to 'What is it?' – what is said in answer to 'What is it?' is not said in answer to 'Which thing is it in its essence?' according to the convention of the people of rational discourse. And the validity of their falling under the answer to 'Which thing?' according to language does not harm us because our speech is in their terminology. Another [response] in repelling the mentioned problem. More subtle because it observes the meaning of the differentia and the state of the questioner seeking it, that he knows the genus first then seeks a differentia. And more precise due to safety from the criticism directed at the response of 'Allama al-Razi – may God have mercy on him – which is that the answer 'the people of rational discourse stipulated thus, and there is no quarrel over terminology' is a response in the manner of the people of rational discourse. [He answered] with 'rational' because the genus is already known, so there is no need to answer with it alone nor with its combination with 'rational'. If you say: 'Rational' meaning 'apprehender of universals' is not specific to man because the Exalted Creator and other abstract entities like intellects and celestial souls also apprehend universals, so it cannot be a proximate differentia for man because they have established that the proximate differentia must be specific to the quiddity for which it is a differentia. And even if conceded that the proximate differentia does not have to be specific to that quiddity, then making it a differentia for man is no more suitable than making it a genus for him. Rather it is possible to make 'animal' a differentia or 'rational' a genus, for each of them is shared between the quiddity of man and others. I say: What is meant by 'rational' is the possessor of the principle of speech and perception, and there is no doubt that that principle is specific to the quiddity of man who is the effect of that principle, so there is no problem.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines the differentia (al-fasl) and addresses the problem that its definition might also apply to the complete definition (al-hadd al-tamm) and the genus. The author begins by stating the standard definition: the differentia is what is predicated in answer to 'What is it in its essence?' This distinguishes the species from others sharing the same genus. However, if one asks about man 'What is he in his essence?', one could answer 'rational animal' (the complete definition) or just 'rational' (the differentia). This causes two problems: (1) the complete definition would then fall under the definition of differentia, but it is not a differentia because it is composite; (2) the definition of differentia is not exclusive since it applies to the complete definition. The author then clarifies that the sought distinction is essential but partial, so only the differentia (a single term) truly distinguishes essentially, while the genus and complete definition distinguish only through the differentia. Two solutions are presented: from the author of al-Muhakamat (Qutb al-Din al-Razi), who argues that in logical terminology 'ayy' seeks a distinguisher that is not predicated in answer to 'What is it?', thus excluding the genus and complete definition; and from al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi, who argues that we first know the genus and then ask for the differentia within that genus (e.g., 'Which animal is man?'), so the answer is only the differentia. The passage ends by addressing an objection: 'rational' might not be specific to man because God and celestial beings also apprehend universals. The response is that 'rational' here means 'possessor of the principle of speech and perception', which is unique to humans.

Checkpoint
What is al-Tusi's main insight regarding the differentia?
A) The differentia is a linguistic convention.
B) The differentia is known only after the genus.
C) The differentia must be composite.
D) The differentia is not necessary.

Key Takeaway
Al-Tusi's solution that the questioner first knows the genus and then seeks the differentia within it provides a natural and precise answer to the overlap problem.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Practise al-Tusi's method: Take the concept 'ijtihad' (independent legal reasoning). First, state its genus (e.g., a type of reasoning effort). Then ask: 'Which reasoning effort is ijtihad in its essence?' Answer with the differentia: 'the total expenditure of effort in seeking a legal ruling from the sources'. Explain why the differentia alone is sufficient.
